<!-- link1 "Item&nbsp;2.01. Completion of Acquisition or Disposition of Assets" -->
<DIV align="left"><A NAME="000"></A></DIV>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Item&nbsp;2.01. Completion of Acquisition or Disposition of Assets.</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This Form 8-K/A is being filed to amend the Form 8-K filed on July&nbsp;29,
2004 by American Medical Systems Holdings, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) to include the
financial statements and financial information referred to in Item&nbsp;9.01 below
which relate to the acquisition of TherMatrx, Inc., a Delaware corporation
(&#147;TherMatrx&#148;) by American Medical Systems, Inc. (&#147;AMS&#148;), a wholly owned
subsidiary of the Company.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On July&nbsp;15, 2004, AMS completed the previously announced acquisition of
TherMatrx. Pursuant to the Agreement and Plan of Merger, dated as of June&nbsp;15,
2004, among AMS; Leio Acquisition Corp., a Delaware corporation and wholly
owned subsidiary of AMS (&#147;Merger Subsidiary&#148;); TherMatrx; TherMatrx Investment
Holdings LLC and BSD Medical Corporation, principal stockholders; and TherMatrx
Investment Holdings LLC, as stockholders&#146; representative, Merger Subsidiary
merged with and into TherMatrx, with TherMatrx surviving and continuing as a
wholly-owned subsidiary of AMS.

<!-- link1 "Item&nbsp;2.02. Results of Operations and Financial Condition" -->
<DIV align="left"><A NAME="001"></A></DIV>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Item&nbsp;2.02. Results of Operations and Financial Condition.</B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">On July&nbsp;29, 2004, the Company issued a press release announcing results for its
second quarter of fiscal year 2004. Attached hereto as Exhibit&nbsp;99.4 is a copy
of the Company&#146;s press release dated July&nbsp;29, 2004 announcing the Company&#146;s
results of operations.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The information contained under this Item&nbsp;2.02 and Exhibit&nbsp;99.4 hereto shall
not be deemed &#147;filed&#148; for purposes of Section&nbsp;18 of the Securities Exchange Act
of 1934, as amended (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;), or incorporated by reference in any
filing under the Securities Act of 1933, as amended, or the Exchange Act,
except as shall be expressly set forth by specific reference in such a filing.


<!-- link1 "Item&nbsp;9.01. Financial Statements and Exhibits" -->
<DIV align="left"><A NAME="002"></A></DIV>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Item&nbsp;9.01. Financial Statements and Exhibits.</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(a)&nbsp;<I>Financial statements of businesses acquired. </I>The financial statements
of TherMatrx are attached hereto as Exhibits 99.1 and 99.2 and are incorporated
herein by reference.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;<I>Pro forma financial information. </I>The pro forma financial information
is attached hereto as Exhibit&nbsp;99.3 and is incorporated herein by reference.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(c)&nbsp;<I>Exhibits</I>. The following materials are filed as exhibits to this
current report on Form 8-K/A.

<DIV align="center">

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><IMG src="c88445c8844500.gif" alt="(BENHAM, ICHEN &#038; KNOX, LLP LETTERHEAD)">

We have audited the financial statements of Thermatrx, Inc. as of September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002
and for the periods then ended for the purpose of expressing an
opinion as to whether the
financial statements present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position, results of
operations, and cash flows of Thermatrx, Inc. in conformity with generally accepted
accounting principles.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">We give permission for the
use of our audit reported dated November&nbsp;10, 2003, except for Note
12 as to which the date is July&nbsp;28, 2004, to be used in the filing of Form&nbsp;8K.

<P align="right" style="font-size: 10pt">EXHIBIT 99.1


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><IMG src="c88445c8844500.gif" alt="(BENHAM, ICHEN &#038; KNOX, LLP LETTERHEAD)">



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>INDEPENDENT AUDITORS&#146; REPORT</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">To the Board of Directors<BR>
TherMatrx, Inc.<BR>
Northbrook, IL 60062

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">We have audited the accompanying balance sheets of TherMatrx, Inc. as of
September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, and the related statements of income and retained
earnings and cash flows for the years then ended. These financial statements
are the responsibility of the Company&#146;s management. Our responsibility is to
express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audits.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">We conducted our audits in accordance with auditing standards generally
accepted in the United States of America. Those standards require that we plan
and perform the audits to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the
financial statements are free of material misstatement. An audit includes
examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in
the financial statements. An audit also includes assessing the accounting
principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as
evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. We believe that our
audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">In our opinion, the financial statements referred to above present fairly, in
all material respects, the financial position of TherMatrx, Inc. as of
September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, and the results of its operations and its cash
flows for the years then ended in conformity with accounting principles
generally accepted in the United States of America.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;<BR>
Sincerely,


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Benham, Ichen &#038; Knox LLP



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">November&nbsp;10, 2003, except for Note 12<BR>
as to which the date is July&nbsp;28, 2004

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>TherMatrx, Inc.<BR>
Notes to Financial Statements<BR>
Years Ended September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 1 &#151; ORGANIZATION AND OPERATION</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">TherMatrx, Inc. (the Company) was incorporated in the state of Delaware on
November&nbsp;13, 1997. The Company is marketing a new medical device to treat
Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia (BPH), which is a non-cancerous enlargement of the
prostate gland. The Company is doing business throughout the United States.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 2 &#151; SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Method of Accounting


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company prepares its financial statements using the accrual basis of
accounting in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles accepted
in the United States of America.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Cash and Cash Equivalents


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Cash and cash equivalents include all monies in banks and highly liquid
investments with maturity dates of less than 60&nbsp;days.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Inventory


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Inventories are stated at the lower of cost or market.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Property and Equipment


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Property and Equipment are carried at cost. Depreciation is provided using the
straight-line method at rates based on the following useful lives:


<DIV align="center">

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Expenditures for major renewals and betterments that extend the useful lives of
property and equipment are capitalized. Expenditures for maintenance and
repairs are charged to expense as incurred.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Use of Estimates


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The process of preparing financial statements in conformity with generally
accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and
assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and
disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial
statements and reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reported
period. Actual results could differ from those estimates.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Advertising


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company expenses advertising costs as they are incurred.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 2 &#151; SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES (CONTINUED)</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Income Taxes


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Income taxes are accounted for in accordance with the provisions of Statement
of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;109. The provision for income tax
expense or benefit is based on income or loss reported for financial statement
purpose adjusted for temporary and permanent differences between reported
financial and taxable income or loss. The Federal Net Operating Loss, at
September&nbsp;30, 2003 totals $7,367,458 and can be used to offset taxable income.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Revenue Recognition


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Revenue is generally recognized when products are shipped. For equipment
shipped to a customer for evaluation, revenue is recognized when the customer
signs a contract to purchase the equipment that has been delivered. (See Note
12)


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Patents


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Patents are amortized on the straight-line basis over 15&nbsp;years.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Rent expense for the years ended September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, was $99,550 and

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company has entered into several consulting agreements with doctors to
provide services on an hourly or fixed fee basis. Consulting fees, charged to
expense for the years ended September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, were $224,750 and
$208,947, respectively.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 4 &#151; INVESTMENT</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Investment consists of a time deposit worth $10,424. The carrying value of
this investment approximates fair value because of the short-term maturity of
this financial instrument. This investment is collateral for an open line of
credit with a third party.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 5 &#151; CONCENTRATION OF CREDIT RISK</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company maintains cash accounts in two financial institutions. Balances in
these accounts exceed the federally insured limit of $100,000.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 6 &#151; RELATED PARTY</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company has entered into a consulting and non-compete, non-disclosure
agreement with BSD Medical Corporation (BSD). BSD owns 78% of the Company&#146;s
common stock.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Consulting Agreement


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company will use the expertise, on an &#147;as needed&#148; basis, of employees of
BSD in the development and monitoring the &#147;FDA&#148; compliance regulations of a
medical device to treat Benign Prostatic Hyperplasia. For the years ended
September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, the Company has paid approximately $230,000 and
$292,000 for these services, respectively.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Other


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company purchased inventory and equipment from BSD totaling $1,161,007 and
$1,856,031 for the years ended September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002. Included in
Accounts Payable is the amount due to BSD of $70,702.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Non-compete, Non-disclosure Agreement


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">BSD has entered into an agreement with the Company not to engage in any
business or provide any services in the treatment of any benign conditions or
diseases of the prostrate gland. BSD shall not disclose any &#147;Confidential
Information&#148; of the clinical trials or the medical device used in such
treatments.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 7 &#151; LINE OF CREDIT</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company has two lines of credit with a commercial bank which provide
borrowings up to $1,000,000 and $1,200,000.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The $1,000,000 line of credit bears interest at a variable rate, the Wall
Street Journal prime, and is payable monthly. The balance outstanding at
September&nbsp;30, 2003 was $0.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The $1,200,000 line of credit bears interest at a variable rate, the Wall
Street Journal prime, and is payable monthly. The balance outstanding at
September&nbsp;30, 2003 was $0.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Both of the lines of credit are secured by certain assets of the Company and a
personal guarantee of certain officers.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The agreement with the bank contains covenants which require the Company to
achieve certain minimum performance levels. As of September&nbsp;30, 2003 the
Company is in compliance with these covenants.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Common and Preferred Stock


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Board of Directors has unanimously approved, at the October&nbsp;19, 2001
meeting, that the total number of shares of stock which the Corporation shall
have authority to issue will be increased to twenty million (20,000,000) shares
each having a par value of $.001 per share, divided into (a)&nbsp;fourteen million
(14,000,000) shares of common stock (the &#147;Common Stock&#148;) and (b)&nbsp;six million
(6,000,000) shares of preferred stock (the &#147;Preferred Stock).


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Stock Options


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company has a stock option plan that allows the Board of Directors to grant
incentive stock options to employees and nonqualified stock options to
employees and consultants of the company. This plan was originally approved in
1997, and was amended and restated in October of 2000. A total of 1,750,000
shares of stock were reserved for issuance under this plan. As of September
30, 2003 there were 109,209 shares available for future grants. Options expire
ten years after the date of grant and are subject to varying vesting schedules.

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Valuation of Intangibles


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">In order to establish the value of the patents and patent rights contributed,
the Company compared the percentage of the shares acquired for cash with the
percentage acquired for the rights to the patents. Based on the expectation
that the &#147;Milestone Closing&#148; would be achieved, it was determined that the
intangible assets contributed were worth $4,000,000 (Note 2). This asset is
shown in the financial statements, as Patents, Net, and it will be amortized
over 15&nbsp;years in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. The
patents and patent rights were contributed to the Company for common stock
valued at $4,000,000.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 9 &#151; RETIREMENT PLAN</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company maintains a SIMPLE retirement plan which allows for employee salary
deferral contributions as well as employer contributions. Employees must meet
certain compensation requirements to participate in the plan. Participants are
vested 100% in both the employee salary deferral and the employer contribution.
The employer contributions for the years ended September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002,
were $88,269 and $43,307, respectively.



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">15
</DIV>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">




<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>TherMatrx, Inc.<BR>
Notes to Financial Statements<BR>
Years Ended September&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 10 &#151; ECONOMIC DEPENDENCY</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company purchases from two vendors, of which one is a related party, the
control boxes of the TMX 2000 System.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The Company purchases all applicators from one supplier.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 11 &#150; OTHER INCOME</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Other income is primarily derived from licensing of certain company owned
patents.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 12 &#150; REVENUE RESTATEMENT</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">In July of 2004, the stock of Thermatrx, Inc. was sold to a third party. The
revenue recognition policy of the acquiring company is different than that of
Thermatrx, Inc. The financial statements for the years ended September&nbsp;30, 2003
and 2002 have been restated to reflect the revenue recognition policy of the
acquiring company.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The acquiring company recognizes revenue when legal title to the good passes to
its customers. The company reports sales net of estimated returns and
discounts. Revenues from equipment sales are generally recognized when the
equipment has been shipped and installed. Certain equipment sales occur under
a contract, which includes combined pricing on both the equipment and
consumable products. In these cases, a portion of revenue and related cost on
the equipment in the contract is recognized as consumable products are shipped
over the life of the contract.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The adjustment for the year ended September&nbsp;30, 2003 decreased income by
$5,452, increased deferred cost by $13,444, and increased deferred revenue by
$7,992.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The adjustment for the year ended September&nbsp;30, 2002 decreased income by
$88,915, increased deferred cost by $265,585, and increased deferred revenue by
$354,500.

<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">




<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>TherMatrx, Inc.<BR>
Notes to Financial Statements<BR>
Periods Ended June&nbsp;30, 2004 and June&nbsp;30, 2003<BR>
(Unaudited)</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 1 &#151; ORGANIZATION AND OPERATION</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">TherMatrx, Inc. was incorporated in the state of Delaware on November&nbsp;13, 1997.
TherMatrx is marketing a new medical device to treat Benign Prostatic
Hyperplasia (BPH), which is a non-cancerous enlargement of the prostate gland.
TherMatrx is doing business throughout the United States.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The financial statements included in this Form 8-K have been prepared by
TherMatrx, Inc., without audit. Certain information and footnote disclosures
normally included in financial statements prepared in accordance with generally
accepted accounting principles have been condensed or omitted pursuant to these
rules and regulations. The year-end balance sheet was derived from audited
financial statements, but does not include all disclosures required by
generally accepted accounting principles. These unaudited interim financial
statements should be read in conjunction with the TherMatrx&#146;s financial
statements and related notes included elsewhere in this Form 8-K/A.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">These statements reflect, in management&#146;s opinion, all adjustments (which
include only normal, recurring adjustments) necessary for a fair presentation
of the financial position and the results of operations and cash flows for the
periods presented. The results of operations for any interim period may not be
indicative of results for the full year.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTE 2 &#151; SUMMARY OF SIGNIFICANT ACCOUNTING POLICIES</B>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Revenue Recognition


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Revenue is generally recognized when products are shipped. For equipment
shipped to a customer for evaluation, revenue is recognized when the customer
signs a contract to purchase the equipment that has been delivered.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The company recognizes revenue when legal title to the good passes to its
customers. The company reports sales net of estimated returns and discounts.
Revenues from equipment sales are generally recognized when the equipment has
been shipped and installed. Certain equipment sales occur under a contract,
which includes combined pricing on both the equipment and consumable products.
In these cases, a portion of revenue and related cost on the equipment in the
contract is recognized as consumable products are shipped over the life of the
contract.

presented for illustrative purposes only and are not necessarily indicative of
the combined financial position or results of operations for future periods or
the financial position or results of operations that actually would have been
realized had American Medical Systems Holdings, Inc. and TherMatrx, Inc. been a
combined company during the specified periods. The unaudited pro forma
condensed combined financial statements, including the related notes, are
qualified in their entirety by reference to, and should be read in conjunction
with, the historical financial statements and related notes of American Medical
Systems Holdings, Inc., included in its Annual Report on Form 10-K and
Quarterly Report on Form 10-Q filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission
on March&nbsp;17, 2004, and August&nbsp;12, 2004, respectively, and the historical
audited financial statements and related notes of TherMatrx, Inc., included
elsewhere in this Form 8-K/A.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">The following unaudited pro forma condensed financial statements are accounted
for in accordance with Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;141,
&#147;Business Combinations&#148;. The pro forma adjustments are based upon preliminary
estimates and available information. Final purchase accounting adjustments may
differ from the pro forma adjustments presented. The pro forma condensed
combined financial statements are based on the respective historical financial
statements of American Medical Systems Holdings, Inc. and TherMatrx, Inc. and
assumes the acquisition took place on January&nbsp;4, 2004, and December&nbsp;29, 2003,
for the statements of operations, and July&nbsp;3, 2004, for the balance sheet. The
pro forma adjustments are based on the estimates and assumptions set forth in
the notes to such pro forma financial statements.

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="right" style="font-size: 10pt">EXHIBIT 99.4


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">DATE: July&nbsp;29, 2004


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>American Medical Systems Reports Record $49.1 Million<BR>
Sales with 33 Percent Net Income Growth in Second Quarter</B>



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Second Half Revenues, Aided by TherMatrx<BR>
Acquisition, Expected to Increase by Over 25%</I>


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">MINNEAPOLIS, July&nbsp;29, 2004 &#150; American Medical Systems Holdings Inc. (NASDAQ:
AMMD) reported another sales record of $49.1&nbsp;million in the second quarter of
2004, a 16&nbsp;percent increase over sales of $42.2&nbsp;million in the comparable
quarter of 2003 (14&nbsp;percent without gain from currency exchange rate changes).
Net income in the quarter was $8.4&nbsp;million, or $0.24 per share, up 33&nbsp;percent
from $6.3&nbsp;million, or $0.19 per share, in the comparable quarter of 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Sales for the first six months of 2004 were $96.4&nbsp;million, up 18% from sales of
$81.6&nbsp;million in 2003 (16&nbsp;percent without gain from currency exchange rate
changes). Net income in the six month period totaled $16.5&nbsp;million, or $0.47
per share, up 40% from $11.8&nbsp;million, or $0.35 per share in 2003.


<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Douglas W. Kohrs, Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of American Medical
Systems, commented, &#147;Our worldwide ability to leverage across our broad product
portfolio was again clear in the second quarter. Women&#146;s continence products
led our growth at 52% above 2003&#146;s comparable period. Male continence
continued its momentum with a 17% increase in the quarter. Erectile
restoration revenue was even with last year&#146;s second quarter, but is poised to
resume growth following the FDA&#146;s clearance of our <I>AMS 700 Tactile Pump</I>&#153;
announced earlier this week. Our TherMatrx acquisition closed early in the
third quarter, thereby giving us another growth engine, and providing us the
opportunity to work directly with our urology customers in meeting the needs of
the high-growth, in-office benign prostatic hyperplasia market.&#148;



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Outlook</B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Inclusive of its recently closed acquisition of TherMatrx, AMS expects 2004
revenue to be in the range of $205 to $210&nbsp;million, generating EPS of $0.95 to
$0.99. For the third quarter of 2004, the Company expects revenue to be in the
range of $49 to $51&nbsp;million. EPS for the third quarter is anticipated in the
range of $0.22 to $0.24.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Earnings Call Information</B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">American Medical Systems will host a conference call today at 5:00 p.m. (EST)
to discuss its second quarter 2004 results. To access the call within the
U.S., dial (800)&nbsp;309-5451, outside the U.S., (706)&nbsp;679-3605. A live web cast
of the call will be available through the Company&#146;s corporate website at
www.AmericanMedicalSystems.com and available for replay two hours after the
completion of the call.



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">&nbsp;
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>About American Medical Systems</B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">American Medical Systems, headquartered in Minnetonka, Minnesota is a
diversified supplier of medical devices and procedures to cure erectile
dysfunction, benign prostatic hyperplasia, incontinence, and other pelvic
disorders in men and women. Although not life threatening, these disorders can
significantly diminish one&#146;s quality of life and profoundly affect social
relation-ships. In recent years, the number of people seeking treatment has
increased markedly as a result of longer lives, higher quality-of-life
expectations and greater awareness of new treatment alternatives. American
Medical Systems&#146; products reduce or eliminate the incapacitating effects of
these diseases, often through minimally invasive therapies. The Company&#146;s
products were used to treat over 100,000 patients in 54 countries during the
last year. More information about the Company and its products may be found at
www.AmericanMedicalSystems.com.



<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>Forward Looking Statements</B>

<P align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Statements about the Company&#146;s future product availability and sales are
forward-looking statements subject to risks and uncertainties including the
timing and success of new product introductions, physician acceptance,
endorsement, and use of the Company&#146;s products, competitor activities, changes
in reimbursement rates, and potential product recalls. These risks and others
are more fully described in the Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form 10-K for the
year ended January&nbsp;3, 2004, and its other SEC filings. Actual results may
differ materially from anticipated results.
